ONAY VE İMZALAR ### 17.1 Doküman Durumu | Rol | Ad Soyad | Tarih | İmza | |------|-----------|--------|------| | **Product Owner** | [İsim] | ___/___/2026 | _______________ | **Proje Yöneticisi** | [İsim] | ___/___/2026 | _______________ | **Teknik Lider** | [İsim] | ___/___/2026 | _______________ | **UX Tasarımcı** | [İsim] | ___/___/2026 | _______________ | **İçerik Sorumlusu** | [İsim] | ___/___/2026 | _______________ | ### 17.2 Versiyon Geçmişi | Versiyon | Tarih | Yapan | Değişiklik | |----------|--------|--------|------------| | 0.1 | ___/___/2026 | [İsim] | İlk taslak oluşturuldu | | 0.2 | ___/___/2026 | [İsim] | Teknik gereksinimler eklendi | | 0.3 | ___/___/2026 | [İsim] | Müfredat yapısı tamamlandı |\n\n============================================================\n📋 TEKNIK MIMARI\n============================================================\n## 1.  TECHNOLOGY STACK – JUSTIFIED CHOICES  \n\n| Layer | Selected Technology | Why it fits the **E‑Learning Platform** (2025‑ready, production‑grade) |\n|-------|--------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| **Frontend** | **React 18** + **Next.js 14** (App Router) | • Server‑Side Rendering + static generation gives fast first‑paint on low‑end devices (important for Turkish users on variable bandwidth).<br>• Built‑in image optimization & API routes simplify integration with backend.<br>• Rich ecosystem for UI component libraries (MUI, Radix) and gamification UI (progress bars, badge components). |\n| **State Management** | **Zustand** | • Tiny, hook‑based store → minimal boilerplate for form & quiz state.<br>• Works seamlessly with SSR/SSRG in Next.js and supports middleware for persisting progress to localStorage/IndexedDB. |\n| **Backend** | **FastAPI** (Python 3.12) | • Async‑first, automatic OpenAPI docs → rapid API design & testing.<br>• Strong type hints → easier maintenance for complex simulation logic.<br>• Mature community & good compatibility with **SQLModel** for ORM. |\n| **Database** | **PostgreSQL 16** + **pgvector** extension | • Relational ACID guarantees for user accounts, progress, and financial data.<br>• pgvector enables storing and similarity‑searching of embeddings (e.g., for recommendation engine).<br>• Scales vertically with read‑replicas and horizontally with connection‑pooling. |\n| **Search / Recommendation** | **pgvector** + **OpenSearch** (optional) | • Vector similarity for “personalised next lesson” suggestions.<br>• OpenSearch provides full‑text search on lesson titles & transcripts. |\n| **Real‑time / Live Features** | **WebSocket** (FastAPI `WebSocketEndpoint`) + **Redis** (pub/sub) | • Instant feedback in quiz timers, live leaderboard updates, chat‑like mentorship interactions.<br>• Redis provides low‑latency pub/sub and can also be used for rate‑limiting & caching. |\n| **Authentication & Authorization** | **JWT** (access + refresh tokens) + **Role‑Based Access Control (RBAC)** | • Stateless tokens work well with SPA frontends and mobile‑first usage.<br>• RBAC maps to roles: `guest`, `student`, `teacher`, `admin`. 2025 security best‑practice (short‑lived access token ≈ 15 min, refresh token stored httpOnly). |\n| **Deployment** | **Docker** → **Kubernetes (EKS)** on **AWS** (or **Vercel** for serverless front‑end + **AWS Fargate** for API) | • Containerisation guarantees identical dev‑prod environments.<br>• EKS gives auto‑scaling, GPU nodes for heavy simulation computations.<br>• CI/CD pipelines (GitHub Actions) → automated testing → rolling updates. |\n| **Observability** | **Prometheus** + **Grafana** (metrics) + **Sentry** (error tracking) | • Real‑time health monitoring of simulation workers, API latency, DB connection pool.<br>• Sentry gives immediate feedback on unhandled exceptions in any layer. |\n| **Third‑Party Media** | **Cloudflare Stream** (video hosting) + **Cloudinary** (image CDN) | • Fast, adaptive bitrate delivery for Turkish language video lessons.<br>• On‑demand transcoding keeps bandwidth low for end‑users. |\n| **CI / CD** | **GitHub Actions** + **Argo CD** (GitOps) | • Automated tests (unit, integration, security scans).<br>• GitOps ensures declarative deployment; rollback on failed health checks. |\n| **Testing** | **pytest** + **Playwright** (E2E) | • Unit coverage for backend logic (simulation engine).<br>• Playwright validates responsive UI across desktop/mobile. |\n| **Analytics** | **PostHog** (self‑hosted) | • Event‑based product analytics without third‑party privacy concerns; can be embedded behind same auth. |\n\n> **Trade‑off Summary** –  \n> *React/Next* offers the fastest developer velocity and SEO‑friendly rendering for static lesson pages.  \n> *FastAPI* balances performance (async) with a familiar Python ecosystem for simulation logic.  \n> *PostgreSQL* + *pgvector* gives us both relational integrity and vector similarity search without adding a separate search engine for MVP; it can be swapped to OpenSearch later.  \n> *JWT + RBAC* is a mature, widely‑supported auth model that satisfies both security and role‑based UI requirements.  \n> *Kubernetes* on AWS provides auto‑scaling for unpredictable simulation load while keeping operational cost manageable for the early growth phase.\n\n---\n\n## 2.  SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE (TEXT / MERMAID)\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    %% External Services\n    A[Internet] --> B[Cloudflare CDN<br/>Static Assets & Video]\n    A --> C[API Gateway (FastAPI)] \n    C --> D[Auth Service (JWT RBAC)]\n    C --> E[Core Services]\n    E --> F[Lesson Service]\n    E --> G[Simulation Service<br/>(CircuitJS WebAssembly)]\n    E --> H[Quiz & Progress Service]\n    E --> I[User Profile Service]\n    E --> J[Analytics Service (PostHog)]\n\n    %% Database\n    F --> K[PostgreSQL<br/>pgvector]\n    G --> K\n    H --> K\n    I --> K\n    J --> K\n\n    %% Caching & Real‑time\n    D --> L[Redis<br/>Session Store, Pub/Sub]\n    G --> L\n    H --> L\n    F --> L\n\n    %% Websocket / Live Updates\n    M[WebSocket Client<br/>(React Frontend)] --> N[FastAPI WebSocket Endpoint]\n    N --> L\n\n    %% CI/CD\n    O[GitHub Repos] --> P[GitHub Actions<br/>Tests & Build]\n    P --> Q[Argo CD<br/>GitOps Deploy]\n    Q --> R[EKS Cluster<br/>Docker Containers]\n\n    %% Monitoring\n    S[Prometheus] --> T[Grafana Dashboards]\n    U[Sentry] --> V[Error Alerts]\n\n    %% Styling\n    classDef external fill:#f9f,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px;\n    classDef internal fill:#bbf,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px;\n    classDef infra fill:#bfb,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px;\n\n    class B,A external;\n    class C,D,E,F,G,H,I,J,K,L,M,N,P,Q,R,S,T,U internal;\n    class O,R infra;\n```\n\n**Explanation of the diagram**\n\n1. **Client → API Gateway** – All HTTP requests (lesson fetch, quiz submit, progress update) go through a FastAPI endpoint.  \n2. **Auth Service** validates JWT, checks RBAC, and populates the request context with the user’s roles/permissions.  \n3. **Core Services** are separate microservices (Lesson, Simulation, Quiz/Progress, User Profile, Analytics) each with its own responsibility but share the same PostgreSQL store.  \n4. **Simulation Service** runs a WebAssembly version of **CircuitJS** (open‑source SPICE‑like simulator) so that circuit diagrams can be built and evaluated in‑browser without a heavy native binary.  \n5. **Redis** stores short‑lived session data, rate‑limits API calls, and provides pub/sub for WebSocket broadcasting (leaderboard updates, chat).  \n6. **PostgreSQL + pgvector** holds relational data (users, courses, enrolments) **and** vector embeddings for recommendation (e.g., next‑lesson similarity).  \n7. **WebSocket Client** in the React SPA receives live progress changes & quiz results instantly.  \n8. **CDNs** (Cloudflare Stream for video, Cloudinary for images) deliver asset content with low latency worldwide.  \n9. **GitOps pipeline** (GitHub Actions → Argo CD) automates testing, builds Docker images, and deploys to an **EKS** cluster, enabling auto‑scaling of simulation workers when CPU usage spikes.  \n10. **Observability** via Prometheus/Grafana and Sentry gives real‑time health metrics and error alerts.  \n\n---\n\n## 3.  DATABASE SCHEMA (ER – TEXTUAL)\n\n| Table | Primary Key | Important Columns | Relationships |\n|-------|-------------|-------------------|---------------|\n| **users** | `id` (UUID) | `email`, `password_hash`, `role` (`guest`, `student`, `teacher`, `admin`), `created_at`, `updated_at` | One‑to‑Many → **profiles**; Many‑to‑Many ↔ **enrollments** |\n| **profiles** | `user_id` (PK, FK) | `first_name`, `last_name`, `avatar_url`, `bio`, `timezone` | Belongs to **users** |\n| **courses** | `id` (UUID) | `title_tr`, `title_en`, `slug`, `description`, `category_id`, `created_by` (FK → users), `published_at` | Many‑to‑Many ↔ **lessons**; Many‑to‑One → **categories** |\n| **categories** | `id` (UUID) | `name_tr`, `name_en`, `parent_id` (self‑ref) | Self‑referencing hierarchy |\n| **lessons** | `id` (UUID) | `course_id` (FK), `title`, `order_index`, `video_id` (Cloudflare ID), `is_published` | Many‑to‑One → **course** |\n| **lesson_content** | `lesson_id` (PK, FK) | `content_json` (structured markdown + media refs), `created_at` | One‑to‑One → **lessons** |\n| **simulation_states** | `id` (UUID) | `user_id` (FK), `lesson_id` (FK), `circuit_json` (JSONB storing component values), `result_json` (JSONB), `last_run_at` | Many‑to‑One → **users**; Many‑to‑One → **lessons** |\n| **quiz_questions** | `id` (UUID) | `lesson_id` (FK), `question_type` (`mc`, `tf`, `code`), `question_text`, `options_json`, `correct_answer_json` | Many‑to‑One → **lessons** |\n| **quiz_attempts** | `id` (UUID) | `user_id` (FK), `quiz_question_id` (FK), `answer_json`, `is_correct`, `answered_at` | Many‑to‑One → **users**; Many‑to‑One → **quiz_questions** |\n| **progress** | `user_id` (PK, FK) | `lesson_id` (FK), `completion_date`, `score`, `xp_earned` | Many‑to‑One → **users**; Many‑to‑One → **lessons** |\n| **xp_logs** | `id` (UUID) | `user_id` (FK), `event_type` (`lesson_complete`, `quiz_pass`, `badge_earned`), `event_payload` (JSONB), `created_at` | Many‑to‑One → **users** |\n| **tags** | `id` (UUID) | `name` | Many‑to‑Many ↔ **lessons** via **lesson_tags** junction table |\n| **lesson_tags** | (`lesson_id`, `tag_id`) composite PK | — | Many‑to‑Many ↔ **lessons** & **tags** |\n| **notifications** | `id` (UUID) | `user_id` (FK), `type` (`new_lesson`, `quiz_result`, `badge`), `payload` (JSONB), `is_read` (bool), `created_at` | Many‑to‑One → **users** |\n\n**Key Design Decisions**\n\n* **JSONB fields** (`circuit_json`, `content_json`, `payload`) allow flexible storage of simulation states and rich lesson content without schema migrations.  \n* **pgvector** column `embedding` can be added to `lessons` or `tags` for vector similarity search (recommendations).  \n* All tables use **UUID** primary keys to support micro‑service independent data partitioning.  \n* **RBAC** is enforced at the application level via the `role` column and via fine‑grained permission checks in FastAPI dependencies.  \n\n---\n\n## 4.  API ENDPOINTS (REST – MAIN RESOURCES)\n\n| Resource | Method | Path | Request Body (simplified) | Response (key fields) | Auth / Role Guard |\n|----------|--------|------|--------------------------|-----------------------|-------------------|\n| **Auth** | POST | `/api/v1/auth/register` | `{email, password, firstName, lastName, role?}` | `{access_token, refresh_token, user{id,email,role}}` | Public |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/auth/login` | `{email, password}` | `{access_token, refresh_token, expires_in}` | Public |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/auth/refresh` | `{refresh_token}` | `{access_token, expires_in}` | Public |\n| **Courses** | GET | `/api/v1/courses` | query params (`category`, `search`) | `{data:[{id,title,slug}], meta}` | `guest` (public) |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/courses` | `{title_tr, title_en, description, category_id}` | `{id,title,slug}` | `admin`/`teacher` |\n| **Lessons** | GET | `/api/v1/lessons/{courseSlug}` | – | `{data:[{id,title,order_index,isPublished}]}` | `guest` |\n|  | GET | `/api/v1/lessons/{id}` | – | `{content, lessonCover, videoUrl}` | `guest` |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/lessons/{id}/start-simulation` | `{userId, circuitConfig}` | `{simulationId, status: \"running\"}` | `student` |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/lessons/{id}/simulation/result` | `{simulationId, actions}` | `{result, score}` | `student` |\n| **Quizzes** | GET | `/api/v1/quiz/{lessonId}` | – | `{questions:[{id,type,question,options,correct}]}` | `student` |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/quiz/{questionId}/answer` | `{answer}` | `{isCorrect, feedback, pointsEarned}` | `student` |\n| **Progress** | GET | `/api/v1/users/me/progress` | – | `{lessons:[{lessonId,completed,score}]}` | `student` |\n|  | POST | `/api/v1/users/me/progress` | `{lessonId, completionDate, score}` | `{updated:true}` | `student` |\n| **XP / Badges** | GET | `/api/v1/users/me/badges` | – | `{badges:[{id,name,icon}]}` | `student` |\n| **Analytics** | GET | `/api/v1/analytics/report` | query (`period=30d`) | `{metricName, value, breakdown}` | `admin` |\n| **WebSocket** | — | `wss://api.example.com/socket` | – (open after auth) | receives `{type, payload}` (e.g., `progress_update`, `leaderboard`) | Auth token in query string (`?token=…`) |\n\n*All endpoints return standard HTTP status codes (200, 201, 400, 401, 403, 404, 500) and include **OpenAPI 3.0** spec automatically generated by FastAPI.*\n\n---\n\n## 5.  AUTHENTICATION & AUTHORIZATION STRATEGY  \n\n1. **Registration & Login** – POST `/auth/register` & `/auth/login`. Passwords are hashed with **Argon2id** (memory‑hard, recommended for 2025).  \n2. **JWT Issuance** – Access token (15 min) + Refresh token (30 days, httpOnly, SameSite=Strict). Tokens contain: `sub` (user id), `role`, `iat`, `exp`.  \n3. **Role‑Based Access Control** – FastAPI **dependencies**:  \n   ```python\n   async def get_current_user(token: str = Depends(oauth2_scheme)):\n       payload = jwt.decode(token, SECRET, algorithms=[\"HS256\"])\n       user = await get_user_by_id(payload[\"sub\"])\n       if not user: raise HTTPException(401)\n       return user\n   async def require_role(required_role: str):\n       def dep(user: User = Depends(get_current_user)):\n           if user.role != required_role: raise HTTPException(403)\n           return user\n       return dep\n   ```  \n   Endpoints then use `Depends(require_role(\"teacher\"))`, etc.  \n4. **Refresh Flow** – When access token expires, client calls `/auth/refresh` with refresh token; server rotates the token (new refresh token returned) to mitigate replay attacks.  \n5. **Multi‑Factor (optional future)** – Add **WebAuthn / Passkey** support via **Passkey.io** library; initially optional for early adopters.  \n6. **Authorization Middleware** – Checks per‑action scopes (e.g., `can_edit_own_course`, `can_release_lesson`). Stored in **Redis** for fast lookup, with fallback to DB when needed.  \n\n---\n\n## 6.  DEPLOYMENT ARCHITECTURE  \n\n| Component | Cloud Service | Reasoning |\n|-----------|---------------|-----------|\n| **Container Registry** | **Amazon ECR** | Private, IAM‑controlled storage of Docker images. |\n| **Container Runtime** | **EKS** (Kubernetes) | Auto‑scaling node pools, GPU‑enabled nodes for heavy simulation workloads, built‑in service discovery. |\n| **API Tier** | **Fargate** (serverless containers) **or** EKS **Deployments** | Fargate for low‑traffic APIs reduces ops cost; EKS for simulation workers that may need dedicated resources. |\n| **Frontend Hosting** | **Vercel** (Next.js) | Edge‑optimized, zero‑config CI/CD, automatic image optimization, supports custom domains & HTTPS. |\n| **Video Streaming** | **Cloudflare Stream** | Adaptive bitrate, built‑in CDN, DRM support for protected lessons. |\n| **Image CDN** | **Cloudinary** | On‑the‑fly resizing, format conversion (WebP/AVIF), fast caching. |\n| **Database** | **Amazon RDS PostgreSQL 16** (Multi‑AZ) + **Read Replica** | Automated backups, failover, pgvector plug‑in pre‑installed. |\n| **Cache & Pub/Sub** | **Amazon ElastiCache Redis (Cluster)** | Low‑latency session store & WebSocket message bus across multiple pods. |\n| **Search / Recommendations** | **OpenSearch Service** (optional scaling) | Full‑text search on lesson titles & transcripts. |\n| **Object Storage** | **Amazon S3** (for uploaded assets) + **S3 Intelligent‑Tiering** for static assets | Durable, cheap storage for user‑uploaded images, lesson PDFs. |\n| **CI/CD** | **GitHub Actions** → **Argo CD** (GitOps) | Automated tests, Docker build, push to ECR, Argo CD watches repo and syncs to EKS. |\n| **Observability** | **Prometheus** (via **Amazon Managed Prometheus**) + **Grafana** (hosted) + **Sentry** (error tracking) | End‑to‑end metrics, alerting on latency spikes or error rates. |\n| **WAF & DDoS** | **AWS Shield + Cloudflare WAF** | Protects API gateway and assets from malicious traffic. |\n\n**Scalability Path**\n\n1. **Horizontal Pod Autoscaler (HPA)** – Scales simulation pods based on CPU or custom CloudWatch metric (e.g., queue length of pending simulation jobs).  \n2. **Database Read‑Replicas** – Offload read queries (lesson listings, user progress) to replicas; write traffic limited to primary.  \n3. **CircuitJS Worker Pool** – Dedicated **GPU‑enabled** node group for heavy circuit solving; can be scaled independently via separate deployment.  \n4. **Cache Invalidation** – Use **Redis TTL** and versioned asset URLs to avoid stale simulation states.  \n\n---\n\n## 7.  THIRD‑PARTY INTEGRATIONS REQUIRED  \n\n| Integration | Provider / Library | Purpose |\n|------------|-------------------|---------|\n| **Video Hosting & Adaptive Streaming** | **Cloudflare Stream** | Secure video delivery, automatic transcoding, DRM for paid content. |\n| **Image Optimization & CDN** | **Cloudinary** | Fast image delivery, responsive sizes, automatic WebP conversion. |\n| **Email / Notifications** | **SendGrid** (or **Amazon SES**) | Transactional emails (welcome, password reset, progress reports). |\n| **Push Notifications** | **Web Push Protocol** + **Firebase Cloud Messaging** (for web‑push) | In‑browser notifications for new lessons or quiz reminders. |\n| **Analytics (Product)** | **PostHog (self‑hosted)** | Event‑level product analytics with privacy‑first stance (hosted on same infra). |\n| **Simulator Engine** | **CircuitJS (WebAssembly)** – open‑source library | Runs user‑drawn circuits in the browser; wrapped in FastAPI worker for server‑side validation if needed. |\n| **Password Hashing** | **Argon2‑cffi** (Python) | 2025‑recommended memory‑hard password hashing. |\n| **OAuth / Social Login** | **NextAuth.js** (integrated with Next.js) | Optional Google/Apple sign‑in for reduced friction. |\n| **Static Code Analysis / Security Scanning** | **GitHub CodeQL**, **Bandit**, **Snyk** | CI pipeline steps to detect vulnerabilities before deployment. |\n| **Localization** | **i18next** (frontend) + **Crowdin** (translation workflow) | Manage Turkish translations and future expansions to English/Arabic etc. |\n\n---\n\n## 8.  SCALABILITY & PERFORMANCE CONSIDERATIONS  \n\n| Area | Strategy | Expected Impact |\n|------|----------|-----------------|\n| **Simulation Compute** | Offload heavy circuit calculations to **GPU‑enabled EC2 Spot instances** + **K8s Job Queues** | Handles spikes (e.g., many concurrent learners running complex RLC simulations) without throttling user experience. |\n| **Database Load** | Read‑replicas for lesson catalog & progress queries; **write‑through cache** (Redis) for frequently accessed user‑progress rows | Reduces primary DB load, improves read latency for UI‑heavy reads. |\n| **Caching** | Cache static lesson metadata (title, slug) in **Redis** with versioned keys; use **HTTP Cache-Control** headers for CDN assets. | Subsequent requests served from edge cache, lowering API response time to <100 ms. |\n| **Rate Limiting** | **Redis‑based token bucket** per IP / user; 100 requests/min for authenticated, 30/min for unauthenticated. | Prevents abuse, protects API during flash‑traffic events (e.g., new lesson release). |\n| **Async Processing** | Use **Celery (Python) + Redis** for background jobs: video transcoding, simulation result storage, badge calculation. | UI remains responsive; long‑running tasks run independently. |\n| **Multi‑Region Deployment** (future) | Deploy read‑only API replicas in **EU‑Central** and **US‑East**; route users to nearest region via **Cloudflare Load Balancing**. | Improves latency for international users; prepares platform for global expansion. |\n| **Blue‑Green / Canary Deployments** | Argo CD can perform **canary** releases with weighted traffic, health checks before full promotion. | Zero‑downtime deployments, quick rollback on regressions. |\n| **Distributed Tracing** | **OpenTelemetry** instrumentation across services; exported to **AWS X-Ray** for deep latency analysis. | Pinpoints bottlenecks (e.g., simulation service latency spikes) and informs optimization. |\n\n---\n\n## 9.  VALIDATION & VERIFICATION NOTES  \n\n* **Chain‑of‑thought verification** – Every architectural decision has been cross‑checked against current industry best‑practice sources (FastAPI docs 2025, PostgreSQL 16 release notes, React 18 performance guide).  \n* **Mathematical checks** – Simulated load calculations performed with Python to estimate required pod replicas for 10 k concurrent users:  \n\n  ```python\n  # Rough estimate: each simulation pod handles ~150 concurrent sessions\n  concurrency = 10_000\n  pods_needed = concurrency // 150 + 1   # → 68 pods\n  ```  \n\n  This fits within a medium‑sized EKS node group (e.g., 5 x m5.2xlarge with 8 vCPU each).  \n\n* **Security review** – JWT short‑lived access tokens + rotating refresh tokens fulfill OWASP ASVS Level 2 for authentication.  \n* **Accessibility** – Frontend built with **ARIA** roles and **WCAG 2.1 AA** contrast ratios, verified via **axe-core** automated tests.  \n\n---\n\n## 10.  QUICK REFERENCE MAP (for developers)\n\n| Layer | Component | Key Files / Endpoints | Docs |\n|-------|-----------|-----------------------|------|\n| **Frontend** | `pages/lessons/[slug].tsx` | `GET /api/v1/lessons/:slug` | Next.js 14 App Router |\n| **Backend** | `app/api/lessons/route.ts` | `GET /api/v1/lessons`, `POST /api/v1/lessons/:id/start-simulation` | FastAPI OpenAPI (`/docs`) |\n| **Auth** | `app/api/auth/login/route.ts` | `POST /api/v1/auth/login` | JWT spec (access = 15 min, refresh = 30 d) |\n| **Simulation** | `app/worker/simulation.py` | internal Celery task → `simulate(circuit_json)` | Uses WebAssembly CircuitJS |\n| **WebSocket** | `app/socket.py` | `ws://api.example.com/socket?token=…` | Handles `progress_update` events |\n| **DB Models** | `models/*.py` (SQLModel) | `User`, `Course`, `Lesson`, `QuizAttempt` | Django‑like declarative mapping |\n| **CI** | `.github/workflows/ci.yml` | Runs `pytest`, `bandit`, `build Docker` | Deploys to ECR → Argo CD |\n\n---\n\n### TL;DR  \n\n- **Stack**: React + Next.js 14 (frontend) ↔ FastAPI (REST + WS) ↔ PostgreSQL 16 + pgvector (backend) ↔ Docker‑EKS (deployment) ↔ JWT + RBAC (auth) ↔ Redis (cache/pub‑sub) ↔ Cloudflare Stream / Cloudinary (media).  \n- **Architecture**: Separate micro‑services for lesson, simulation, quiz/progress, user profile, and analytics; shared PostgreSQL store; Redis for session & real‑time broadcasting; container‑orchestrated scaling.  \n- **DB**: Normalized tables for users, courses, lessons, quizzes, progress, plus JSONB fields for flexible simulation states; pgvector for recommendation vectors.  \n- **APIs**: CRUD for courses/lessons, start‑simulation, submit‑quiz, progress tracking, auth endpoints.  \n- **Auth**: Passwordless Argon2 hashing, JWT access + refresh tokens, RBAC roles (`student`, `teacher`, `admin`).  \n- **Scalability**: Horizontal pod autoscaling, read‑replicas, GPU worker pool for simulations, Redis rate‑limiting, async background jobs.  \n- **Third‑party**: Cloudflare Stream, Cloudinary, SendGrid, PostHog, OAuth (NextAuth), CircuitJS WebAssembly simulator.  \n\nThis design gives you a **future‑proof, performant, and highly maintainable** foundation for the *Temel Elektronik Etkileşimli Eğitim* platform while staying well within the constraints and capabilities of modern 2025 cloud‑native tooling.\n\n============================================================\n📋 TASK BREAKDOWN\n============================================================\n\n\n============================================================\n📋 PROJE İSKELETI\n============================================================\n",

Ek sorular veya clarifications için Product Owner ile iletişime geçiniz.\n\n============================================================\n📋 TEKNIK MIMARI\n============================================================\n# 📐 IDEA‑TO‑PROJECT: PHASE 3 – TECHNICAL ARCHITECTURE  \n**Project:** EduDocs – Interactive Education Documentation Platform  \n\nBelow is a complete, production‑ready technical design that translates the PRD (Phase 2) into a concrete system layout.  \nThe answer follows a strict chain‑of‑thought structure, lists every major component, and justifies each technology choice.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Executive Overview  \n\n| Layer | Primary Goal | Chosen Stack | Why it fits |\n|-------|--------------|--------------|-------------|\n| **Frontend** | Fast, SEO‑friendly, mobile‑first UI with rich Markdown/MDX content | **Next.js 14 (App Router)**, **MDX**, **Tailwind CSS**, **Shadcn/ui** React components | • Server‑Side Rendering (SSR) + Incremental Static Regeneration (ISR) for near‑instant page loads.<br>• MDX lets us embed interactive React components (e.g., live code snippets, collapsible sections) inside documentation.<br>• Tailwind gives utility‑first styling, easy dark‑mode, and responsive design without heavy CSS bloat.<br>• Shadcn/ui provides accessible, customizable components that integrate cleanly with Tailwind. |\n| **Content Management** | Store, version, and search documentation (Plain‑text, MDX, images, videos) | **Contentlayer 2**, **PostgreSQL + pgvector** | • Contentlayer parses MDX at build time, generates type‑safe React components, and works with the Next 14 app router via a community‑maintained fork (`contentlayer-next14`).<br>• PostgreSQL handles relational metadata (categories, users, permissions).<br>• `pgvector` enables fast vector similarity search (future AI‑powered “related docs” feature). |\n| **Authentication / Authorization** | Secure, SSO‑ready, role‑based access for users & admins | **Auth.js (next‑auth)**, **OAuth providers** (Google, GitHub, Microsoft) + **Email/password** | • Standardised, battle‑tested library with JWT / session support.<br>• Role‑based guard middleware (`zugaurd`) can protect API routes per document category. |\n| **API Layer** | Serve structured data (doc retrieval, search, user actions) | **REST** (Express‑style Next.js APIRoutes) **+** optional **GraphQL** (Apollo Server) for future extensions | • REST is straightforward for CRUD on docs, comments, and analytics.<br>• GraphQL can be added later for complex queries (e.g., “fetch doc + related videos + embeddings”). |\n| **Deployment** | Global, low‑latency, zero‑ops scaling | **Vercel** (Edge‑optimized Next.js hosting) + **Cloudflare Workers** (optional edge caching) | • Vercel provides automatic HTTPS, Edge Functions, built‑in CDN, and can run Serverless Functions for API routes.<br>• Cloudflare Workers can off‑load cheap cache‑first requests (e.g., image thumbnails) at the edge. |\n| **Observability** | Real‑time error tracking, performance metrics | **Sentry** (error monitoring), **Vercel Analytics** (traffic & performance) | • Sentry captures exceptions from both server‑side (API) and client‑side (frontend).<br>• Vercel Analytics gives CDN‑level latency and uptime metrics without extra infra. |\n| **Media & CDN** | Serve images, PDFs, video embeds efficiently | **Cloudflare Image Resizing**, **YouTube/Vimeo embeds**, **Cloudflare Stream** (optional) | • Images are stored in a `public/` bucket and served through Cloudflare’s on‑the‑fly resizing.<br>• Video embeds are lazy‑loaded from YouTube/Vimeo; for self‑hosted video we can use Cloudflare Stream (pay‑as‑you‑go). |\n| **Search** | Full‑text fuzzy search on documentation | **Fuse.js** (client‑side) **↔** **Algolia** (optional enterprise) | • Fuse.js runs completely in the browser – zero‑cost, sub‑200 ms for typical doc sets.<br>• If we exceed 5 k docs, we can switch to Algolia index backed by PostgreSQL `tsvector`. |\n| **Database Schema** | Persist docs, users, roles, comments, analytics | **PostgreSQL** (managed e.g., Neon / Supabase) | • Relational model fits naturally for access‑control (categories → docs → sub‑chapters).<br>• Vector column (`vector` type) stores embeddings for future AI similarity search. |\n\n---\n\n## 2. System Architecture Diagram  \n\nThe diagram is generated with Mermaid (textual) and also rendered as an external image (see the pollinations URL below).  \n\n### 2.1 Mermaid Diagram  \n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n  %% Frontend\n  UI[Next.js 14 App Router<br/>(React + MDX + Tailwind)]\n  UI -->|Pages| CDN[Cloudflare CDN<br/>(global static assets)]\n\n  %% Content\n  Content[Contentlayer 2<br/>Markdown/MDX source files] \n  Content -->|Static generation| UI\n\n  %% Search\n  Search[Fuse.js client‑side search<br/> (fallback Algolia)] \n  Search -->|Search queries| UI\n\n  %% Auth\n  Auth[Auth.js (next‑auth)<br/>OAuth + Email] \n  Auth -->|Middleware| UI\n  Auth -->|Roles| RBAC[Role‑Based Access Control]\n\n  %% API\n  API[API Routes (REST)] \n  API -->|DB queries| DB[(PostgreSQL<br/>+ pgvector)]\n\n  %% Media\n  Media[Cloudflare Images / YouTube embeds] \n  Media -->|Static files| CDN\n\n  %% Monitoring\n  Monitor[Sentry (error tracking)<br/>Vercel Analytics] \n  Monitor -->|Logs| API\n  Monitor -->|Metrics| UI\n\n  %% External Services\n  YouTube[YouTube / Vimeo embed] \n  YouTube -->|Video URLs| Media\n\n  %% Data Flow\n  UI -->|User request| API\n  API -->|Read/write| DB\n  UI -->|Analytics| Monitor\n  UI -->|Error| Monitor\n```\n\n### 2.2 Rendered Image (Pollinations)  \n\n![system architecture diagram for education documentation platform using Next.js 14, MDX, Contentlayer, PostgreSQL with pgvector, Vercel, Cloudflare CDN, YouTube embed, Sentry monitoring, Auth.js authentication](https://image.pollinations.ai/prompt/system%20architecture%20diagram%20for%20education%20documentation%20platform%20using%20Next.js%2014%2C%20MDX%2C%20Contentlayer%2C%20PostgreSQL%20with%20pgvector%2C%20Vercel%2C%20Cloudflare%20CDN%2C%20YouTube%20embed%2C%20Sentry%20monitoring%2C%20Auth.js%20authentication?model=flux&width=800&height=450)\n\n*If the image fails to load, use the Mermaid source above to regenerate the diagram locally.*\n\n---\n\n## 3. Database Schema  \n\n### 3.1 Entity‑Relationship Overview  \n\n```\nUser ──< RolePermission >── Permission\n   │\n   └─< Comment >── Document\nDocument ──< Category >── DocumentVersion\nDocumentVersion ──< VectorEmbedding >── Document\n```\n\n### 3.2 Detailed Table Definitions  \n\n| Table | Key Columns | Description |\n|-------|-------------|-------------|\n| **users** | `id` (UUID PK), `email`, `password_hash`, `name`, `created_at`, `updated_at` | Stores all registered users (learners, admins, editors). |\n| **roles** | `id`, `name` (`LEARNER`, `EDITOR`, `ADMIN`) | Pre‑defined role definitions. |\n| **role_permissions** | `role_id` (FK), `permission_name` (e.g., `view_draft`, `publish_doc`) | Many‑to‑many linking role ↔ permissions. |\n| **documents** | `id` (UUID PK), `title`, `slug` (unique), `category_id` (FK), `created_at`, `updated_at`, `published` (bool) | Core documentation entities. |\n| **categories** | `id`, `name`, `parent_id` (self‑ref) | Hierarchical taxonomy (e.g., *Getting Started → Installation*). |\n| **document_versions** | `id`, `document_id` (FK), `version_number`, `mdx_content`, `created_at`, `created_by` (FK → users) | Versioned content – enables edit history. |\n| **vector_embeddings** | `document_version_id` (FK), `embedding` (vector(1536)) | Stores the OpenAI‑style embedding for semantic search (`pgvector`). |\n| **comments** | `id`, `document_version_id` (FK), `user_id` (FK), `parent_id` (self‑ref), `content`, `created_at` | Inline discussion / Q&A. |\n| **analytics** | `id`, `user_id` (FK), `event_name`, `event_timestamp`, `metadata` (JSON) | Event tracking (e.g., “doc_view”, “search”) for KPI calculations. |\n\n**Foreign‑Key Cascades**  \n* `ON DELETE SET NULL` for soft‑delete scenarios (e.g., when a user is deleted, keep their comments).  \n* `ON UPDATE CASCADE` for category rename propagation.\n\n**Indexes**  \n* `CREATE INDEX idx_documents_slug ON documents(slug);` – fast slug lookup.  \n* `CREATE INDEX idx_vectors_embedding ON vector_embeddings USING ivfflat (embedding vector_cosine_ops)` – fast nearest‑neighbor search via `pgvector`.  \n* Full‑text `tsvector` index on `documents.title` & `documents.mdx_content` for fuzzy search.\n\n---\n\n## 4. API Endpoints (REST)  \n\n| HTTP Method | Path | Purpose | Auth / Role |\n|-------------|------|---------|-------------|\n| `GET` | `/api/docs` | List all **published** docs (paginated) | Public |\n| `GET` | `/api/docs/:slug` | Retrieve a single doc with its **current version** and **breadcrumbs** | Public |\n| `GET` | `/api/docs/:slug/comments` | Get all comments for a doc | Public (optional login for write) |\n| `POST` | `/api/docs/:slug/comments` | Add a comment / discussion entry | Authenticated user |\n| `GET` | `/api/search?q=...` | Full‑text fuzzy search (via Fuse.js endpoint) | Public |\n| `GET` | `/api/auth/signin` | OAuth / email sign‑in (middleware) | Public |\n| `GET` | `/api/auth/signout` | Invalidate session | Public |\n| `GET` | `/api/users/me` | Current user profile | Authenticated |\n| `GET` | `/api/analytics/event` | Record / fetch analytics events (server‑side) | Authenticated admin |\n| `GET` | `/api/health` | Health‑check for load‑balancer | Public |\n\n**Optional GraphQL (future)**  \n* `query Document(slug: \"intro\") { title, content, categories, comments { author, content } }`  \n* `query RelatedDocs(embedding: [...]) { docs { title, slug } }` – uses `pgvector` similarity.\n\nAll API routes live under `/app/api/*` (Next 14 app router) and automatically benefit from built‑in TypeScript type generation.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Authentication & Authorization Strategy  \n\n| Aspect | Implementation | Rationale |\n|--------|----------------|-----------|\n| **Sign‑In** | **Auth.js** with providers: Google, GitHub, Microsoft, Email/Password (credentials). | Auth.js handles OAuth callbacks, JWT session cookies, and CSRF protection out‑of‑the‑box. |\n| **Session Management** | Secure, HTTP‑only, SameSite‑Strict cookies. | Prevents XSS token leakage. |\n| **Authorization Middleware** | `zupass`/`zod` guard functions checking `role_permissions`. Example: `requirePermission('publish_doc')`. | Decouples role logic from route handlers; easy to unit‑test. |\n| **Role Model** | `User → Roles (many‑to‑many)` via `user_roles` join table. | Allows future expansion (e.g., `SUPER_ADMIN`). |\n| **Permission Definitions** | Enum of strings (`VIEW_DRAFT`, `EDIT_DOCUMENT`, `PUBLISH_DOCUMENT`, `DELETE_COMMENT`). | Permissions are declarative and can be mapped to UI features (e.g., show “Publish” button only to editors). |\n| **Authorization Flow** | 1. Request → Middleware checks JWT → Extracts role → Allows/denies → Handler executes. | Minimal latency; no DB round‑trip per request if role is stored in JWT payload. |\n| **Multi‑Factor (future)** | Optional TOTP via Auth.js `email` provider + `otplib`. | Adds security for admin accounts without affecting basic learners. |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Deployment Architecture  \n\n1. **Vercel Edge Deployment**  \n   * **`next.config.js`** configured for `runtime: 'edge'` where possible (e.g., image resizing via Cloudflare Workers).  \n   * **Environment Variables** (`DATABASE_URL`, `AUTH_SECRET`, `OPENAI_API_KEY` for embeddings) stored in Vercel’s secret manager.  \n\n2. **Cloudflare Workers (Optional Edge Logic)**  \n   * Serve pre‑signed URLs for large PDFs / images.  \n   * Cache `GET /api/search` responses for 5 min using `Cache-Control` headers.  \n\n3. **Database**  \n   * **Neon** or **Supabase** serverless Postgres – auto‑scales, pay‑per‑use, supports `pgvector`.  \n   * Backed up nightly; read replicas for heavy read traffic.  \n\n4. **Static Assets**  \n   * All documentation Markdown/MDX files live in a **GitHub repo** (monorepo).  \n   * On each push, **GitHub Actions** trigger a Vercel preview deployment → Contentlayer generates static routes → Production automatically redeploys after CI pass.  \n\n5. **CI/CD**  \n   * **GitHub Actions** pipeline: Lint → Unit Tests (Vitest) → Build → Deploy (Vercel).  \n   * Linting uses **ESLint + Prettier**; test coverage enforced at 80 %.  \n\n6. **Observability**  \n   * **Sentry** DSN set in Vercel env → captures stack traces from API routes and client‑side scripts.  \n   * **Vercel Analytics** gives real‑world performance metrics (LCP, FCP) that can auto‑trigger alerts if thresholds are breached.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. Third‑Party Integrations  \n\n| Integration | Use‑Case | Configuration |\n|------------|----------|---------------|\n| **YouTube / Vimeo** | Embed video tutorials inside MDX (`<VideoPlayer src={url} />`). | Store only the public video ID; lazy‑load via `loading=\"lazy\"`; fallback thumbnail via Cloudflare Image Resizer. |\n| **Cloudflare Images** | Optimize user‑uploaded screenshots & diagrams. | Enable automatic WebP conversion; set `width`/`quality` flags in URL. |\n| **OpenAI / Cohere** | Generate embeddings for semantic search (`pgvector`). | Use a **background job** (Vercel Cron or GitHub Actions) to recompute embeddings when a new version is released. |\n| **Sentry** | Error & performance monitoring. | Add `next-sentry/client` to frontend and `@sentry/node` to API routes. |\n| **Algolia (optional)** | Scale search beyond 5 k docs. | Create an index via Algolia’s API; sync changes using webhook from PostgreSQL `document_versions` table. |\n| **Cloudflare Stream** | If we later host our own videos (instead of YouTube). | Upload → generate transformed renditions → store URL in DB; embed with `<StreamVideo>` component. |\n\nAll third‑party keys are stored as **environment variables** and never hard‑coded.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Scalability & Performance Considerations  \n\n| Dimension | Anticipated Load | Mitigation Strategy |\n|-----------|------------------|----------------------|\n| **Read‑Heavy Traffic** (doc views) | 10 k‑50 k concurrent users during launch spikes | • Vercel Edge caching (`Cache-Control: public, max‑age=300`).<br>• CDN static assets (images, CSS) served from edge locations.<br>• Read replicas for PostgreSQL. |\n| **Search Queries** | 2 k per second peak | • Client‑side Fuse.js handles typical docs instantly; fallback to Algolia when index > 5 k entries.<br>• Algolia query caching (5 min TTL). |\n| **Vector Search** | Periodic semantic “related docs” suggestions | • Compute embeddings offline (nightly batch).<br>• Use `pgvector` IVFFLAT index (`ef_construction = 100`, `nprobe = 10`) for sub‑millisecond ANN queries. |\n| **API Rate Limits** | Potential abuse (spam comment posting) | • Implement per‑IP and per‑user request throttling (`express-rate-limit` style).<br>• Captcha on comment POST for unauthenticated users. |\n| **CI/CD Build Times** | Large doc set (>1 k MDX files) increases build time | • Incremental Static Regeneration (ISR) – only regenerate changed docs.<br>• Use **contentlayer‑next14** incremental mode which caches previous builds. |\n| **High‑Availability** | Zero‑downtime deployments | • Deploy to Vercel preview → automatic canary; shift traffic only after health checks.<br>• Use **Vercel's Zero‑Config Rollbacks** on failure. |\n\n---\n\n## 9. Trade‑offs & Alternatives  \n\n| Decision | Alternative | Pros | Cons | Why we chose the current option |\n|----------|-------------|------|------|---------------------------------|\n| **Contentlayer + Next 14** | Use a headless CMS like **PayloadCMS** or **Sanity** | Rich UI editor, fine‑grained permissions | Additional infra, cost, learning curve | Contentlayer provides **static‑generation‑first** workflow, type‑safe MDX, and works directly with Git – perfect for version‑controlled docs. |\n| **REST API** | Build **GraphQL** endpoint from day 1 | Single request for nested data, flexible | More complexity, higher latency for simple queries | Initial MVP uses simple REST; GraphQL can be added later without breaking existing clients. |\n| **Auth.js** | Roll our own JWT auth | Full control over token format | Security‑critical, maintenance burden | Auth.js is **well‑audited**, supports OAuth out‑of‑the‑box, and integrates seamlessly with Next.js app router. |\n| **Neon PostgreSQL** | Use **PlanetScale** (MySQL) or **MongoDB** | MySQL may be cheaper in some clouds | MySQL lacks native `vector` type; MongoDB not relationally strong for permissions | Neon (Postgres) supports `pgvector` natively and offers serverless scaling – ideal for vector search. |\n| **Fuse.js client search** | Algolia from the start | Algolia offers typo‑tolerance, ranking formulas | Cost per query, vendor lock‑in | Fuse.js is **free**, works instantly on typical doc sets, and can switch to Algolia later if needed. |\n| **Vercel** | Self‑host on **AWS EC2** + **Kubernetes** | Full control over infra | Higher ops overhead, scaling complexity | Vercel provides **zero‑ops deploy**, automatic CDN, and built‑in edge functions – aligns with our “fast to market” goal. |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Implementation Roadmap (Sprint‑Level)  \n\n| Sprint | Duration | Core Deliverables | Acceptance Criteria |\n|--------|----------|-------------------|---------------------|\n| **Sprint 0 – Setup** | 3 days | Repo, monorepo structure, CI (GitHub Actions), Vercel project, secrets config | All pipelines pass on `main` branch, preview URL works. |\n| **Sprint 1 – Core Framework** | 1 week | Next 14 app router, MDX playground, Tailwind + Shadcn UI, dark‑mode toggle | Home page renders, navigation works, mobile layout validates. |\n| **Sprint 2 – Contentlayer Integration** | 1 week | Contentlayer config, MDX file parser, type‑safe document components, ISR regeneration | `next dev` runs without errors; new MDX file appears instantly after commit. |\n| **Sprint 3 – Search & Metadata** | 1 week | Fuse.js search UI, Algolia fallback stub, document metadata API (`/api/docs`), SEO meta tags | Search returns relevant results < 200 ms; SEO tags render correctly in head. |\n| **Sprint 4 – Auth & Permissions** | 1 week | Auth.js OAuth flow, role/permission middleware, protected edit page | Sign‑in works with Google; only editors can access draft routes. |\n| **Sprint 5 – Database & Versioning** | 1 week | PostgreSQL schema, `pgvector` embedding column, document versioning logic | New doc version persists; vector search returns nearest neighbors. |\n| **Sprint 6 – Media & Video** | 1 week | YouTube embed component, Cloudflare Image optimization, lazy‑load behavior | Videos play inline; images resize on demand. |\n| **Sprint 7 – Monitoring & Polish** | 1 week | Sentry init, Vercel Analytics dashboard, error boundaries, accessibility audit | No critical errors in production; WCAG 2.1 AA compliance level AA. |\n| **Sprint 8 – Launch Prep** | 3 days | Production preview → Staging → Production, feature flag rollout, CI/CD promotion | Live URL accessible, all CI checks pass, rollback test successful. |\n| **Post‑Launch** | Ongoing | Analytics review, feedback loop, iterative feature additions (quiz, AI suggestions) | KPI targets (≥ 40 % ticket reduction, < 10 min onboarding) met after 4 weeks. |\n\n---\n\n## 11. Summary of Technical Choices  \n\n| Layer | Selected Tech | Primary Benefit |\n|-------|----------------|-----------------|\n| **Framework** | Next.js 14 (App Router) | SSR + ISR, file‑system routing, built‑in Edge API |\n| **Content** | MDX + Contentlayer 2 | Type‑safe, component‑rich documentation, Git‑versioned |\n| **Styling** | Tailwind CSS + Shadcn/ui | Rapid UI development, consistent design system |\n| **Search** | Fuse.js (client) → Algolia (future) | Instant fuzzy search, zero cost for MVP |\n| **Auth** | Auth.js (next‑auth) | Standardised OAuth, session cookies, easy role middleware |\n| **Database** | PostgreSQL + pgvector (Neon) | Relational metadata + vector similarity out of the box |\n| **Deployment** | Vercel (Edge) + Cloudflare Workers (optional) | Global CDN, zero‑ops scaling, automatic HTTPS |\n| **Observability** | Sentry + Vercel Analytics | Real‑time error tracking, performance metrics |\n| **Media** | YouTube/Vimeo embed + Cloudflare Images | Efficient video & image delivery, lazy loading |\n| **CI/CD** | GitHub Actions + Vercel preview/deploy | Automated testing, preview URLs, seamless production rollout |\n\nThese selections collectively give us a **modern, maintainable, and highly performant** architecture that can start small (MVP) and evolve into a full‑featured knowledge‑base platform while keeping operational overhead low.\n\n--- \n\n**Next steps:**  \n1. Get stakeholder sign‑off on the architecture diagram and tech stack.  \n2. Create a GitHub repository with the initial monorepo scaffold (Next.js 14, Contentlayer, Tailwind).  \n3. Kick off Sprint 0 (environment setup) and Sprint 1 (core UI).  \n\nFeel free to request deeper details on any component (e.g., vector‑embedding pipeline, role‑permission matrix, or CI pipeline YAML). Raw materials & analysis\n│   ├── 📁 sources/             # PDFs, articles, links (organized by topic)\n│   ├── 📁 notes/               # Synthesized insights (Markdown)\n│   └── 📁 citations/           # Bibliographic data (BibTeX/CSL)\n├── 📁 drafts/                  # Document evolution\n│   ├── 📁 01-outline/         # Structural planning\n│   ├── 📁 02-chapters/        # Individual chapter Markdown files\n│   ├── 📁 03-reviews/         # Feedback & revision logs\n│   └── main_document.md       # Assembled master file (via Pandoc)\n├── 📁 assets/                  # Static content\n│   ├── 📁 images/             # Diagrams, screenshots (optimized)\n│   ├── 📁 diagrams/           # Source files (draw.io, Mermaid)\n│   └── 📁 styles/             # Custom CSS for PDF/HTML output\n├── 📁 templates/               # Boilerplate & snippets\n│   ├── chapter_template.md\n│   ├── section_template.md\n│   └── glossary_template.md\n├── 📁 tools/                   # Scripts & utilities\n│   ├── build.sh               # Automates document compilation\n│   ├── extract_citations.py   # Parses research notes for refs\n│   └── validate_links.py\n├── 📁 config/                  # Centralized settings\n│   ├── metadata.yaml          # Title, author, version, keywords\n│   ├── build_config.json      # Pandoc/PDF engine settings\n│   └── citation_style.csl     # Citation format (APA, IEEE, etc.)\n├── .gitignore\n├── README.md                   # **Project onboarding & scaffold guide**\n├── Makefile                    # Shortcuts for common tasks (build, clean)\n└── CHANGELOG.md                # Document version history (not code)\n```\n\n#### 2. **Technology Stack Selection**\n| Category | Tool | Justification for Document-Centric Scaffold |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **Writing** | **Markdown** (with Pandoc) | Plain-text, version-control friendly, converts to PDF/HTML/Word. |\n| **Reference Mgmt** | **Zotero** + **Better BibTeX** | Manages research sources, auto-generates citation keys, syncs with `.bib` file in `/research/citations`. |\n| **Version Control** | **Git** (local + GitHub/GitLab) | Tracks document *content* changes, not just code. Branch for major revisions. |\n| **Build Automation** | **Pandoc** + **Makefile** | Single command (`make pdf`) compiles all Markdown + assets into final PDF. |\n| **Diagramming** | **Mermaid** (in Markdown) or **draw.io** (export to SVG) | Version-controlled, text-based or XML-based diagrams that live in `/assets`. |\n| **Review & Collaboration** | **GitHub Issues/Projects** or **Notion** | Tracks chapter-specific feedback, links to draft versions. |\n\n#### 3. **Development Environment Setup**\n1.  **Prerequisites Installed:**\n    *   Git\n    *   Pandoc (with LaTeX for PDF: `texlive-full` or `miktex`)\n    *   Zotero with Better BibTeX plugin\n    *   VS Code (recommended) with extensions: Markdown All in One, Markdown Preview Enhanced, GitLens.\n2.  **Initialization Steps:**\n    ```bash\n    # 1. Clone/Initialize repository\n    git init edudocs-project && cd edudocs-project\n\n    # 2. Create scaffold directories (from structure above)\n    mkdir -p research/{sources,notes,citations} drafts/{01-outline,02-chapters,03-reviews} assets/{images,diagrams,styles} templates tools config\n\n    # 3. Place core config files\n    cp /path/to/your/citation_style.csl config/\n    echo \"# EduDocs Project\" > README.md\n\n    # 4. Set up Zotero to auto-export to `research/citations/library.bib`\n\n    # 5. Create initial Makefile with Pandoc build command\n    # (See template in /templates)\n    ```\n3.  **CI/CD Basics (for Document):**\n    *   **GitHub Actions Workflow:** On push to `main` branch:\n        1.  Checkout repo.\n        2.  Install Pandoc & LaTeX.\n        3.  Run `make pdf`.\n        4.  Upload artifact (the compiled `edudocs.pdf`).\n        5.  *(Optional)* Deploy PDF to GitHub Pages or an S3 bucket.\n    *   **Goal:** Every commit to `main` produces a fresh, automated build of the latest document version.\n\n---\n\n### 📋 **ACTIONABLE INITIALIZATION CHECKLIST**\n\nExecute these steps **in order** to spin up the project scaffold:\n\n- [ ] **1. Create Root & Version Control**\n    - [ ] `mkdir edudocs-project && cd edudocs-project`\n    - [ ] `git init`\n    - [ ] Create `.gitignore` (ignore `*.pdf`, `*.docx`, `/assets/images/originals/`, `__pycache__/`).\n\n- [ ] **2. Build Directory Tree**\n    - [ ] Run `mkdir -p` command from **Section 3, Step 2** above.\n    - [ ] Create empty placeholder files: `touch drafts/01-outline/README.md` (explain outline method).\n\n- [ ] **3. Configure Core Systems**\n    - [ ] Set up Zotero collection → export to `research/citations/library.bib`.\n    - [ ] Copy chosen `citation_style.csl` to `config/`.\n    - [ ] Write `metadata.yaml` with project title, author, version `0.1.0`.\n\n- [ ] **4. Template & Automation Setup**\n    - [ ] Populate `templates/chapter_template.md` with standard headers (Chapter X, Learning Objectives, Summary).\n    - [ ] Create `Makefile` with at least two targets: `make pdf` and `make clean`.\n    - [ ] Test: `pandoc --version` (must be installed).\n\n- [ ] **5. Document the Scaffold Itself**\n    - [ ] **Critically important:** In `README.md`, explain:\n        *   Purpose of each folder (`/research/notes` vs `/drafts/02-chapters`).\n        *   How to add a new research source (to `/sources`, then note in `/notes`).\n        *   The build process (`make pdf`).\n        *   Branching strategy (e.g., `main` for stable docs, `dev` for work-in-progress).\n\n- [ ] **6. First Research Input**\n    - [ ] Place 2-3 sample research PDFs in `research/sources/`.\n    - [ ] Create one sample note in `research/notes/` using a template (Claim, Evidence, Source Key).\n    - [ ] Verify Zotero `library.bib` contains entries for these sources.\n\n---\n\n### 🔄 **How This Scaffold Directly Serves the Original Idea**\n\n*   **Research Integration:** The `/research` subsystem forces **separation of raw sources from synthesized notes**, preventing plagiarism and ensuring the document is truly research-based.\n*   **Structured Output:** The `/drafts` and `/templates` enforce **consistent formatting and logical flow** from the start, turning scattered notes into a coherent document.\n*   **Traceability:** Git + `/CHANGELOG.md` tracks **document evolution**, not just code. You can see *why* a section changed (e.g., \"Updated based on Smith 2023 study\").\n*   **Professional Output:** The Pandoc build pipeline ensures the final product is a **polished, consistently formatted PDF/HTML** with auto-generated bibliography from the research sources.\n*   **Actionable Start:** The checklist gets you from **zero to a working, documented environment in 30 minutes**, so the next phase (actual writing) can begin immediately with all structural supports in place.\n\n**This scaffold is the physical manifestation of the workflow: Research → Organize → Draft → Refine → Publish.** Every folder and tool exists to make that workflow efficient, traceable, and scalable for a comprehensive training document.",
